<div id="review_107252596" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107252596" />
    <a title="Kricket" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/125201-kricket"><img alt="Kricket" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455408697p2/125201.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107252596?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kricket" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kricket" href="/user/show/125201-kricket">Kricket</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/125201-kricket?shelf=memoir-ish">memoir-ish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/125201-kricket?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/125201-kricket?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/125201-kricket?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/125201-kricket?shelf=marriage">marriage</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107252596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11316222155417201154">my love for this book has a lot to do with who i am and where i am in life, so i don't expect that everyone else will have the same experience when reading it. even though i married young, we are coming on 4 years of what EG describes as husbandless, wifeless, childless marriage. in other words, a bit nontraditional. so this book, which is EG's exploration of whether or not her nontraditional relationship can fit into a traditional state-sanctioned marriage, really spoke to me. <br/><br/>at the end of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19501.Eat__Pray__Love' title='Eat, Pray, Love by Elizabeth Gilbert' rel='nofollow noopener'>eat</a></span>
  <span id="freeText11316222155417201154" style="display:none">my love for this book has a lot to do with who i am and where i am in life, so i don't expect that everyone else will have the same experience when reading it. even though i married young, we are coming on 4 years of what EG describes as husbandless, wifeless, childless marriage. in other words, a bit nontraditional. so this book, which is EG's exploration of whether or not her nontraditional relationship can fit into a traditional state-sanctioned marriage, really spoke to me. <br /><br />at the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19501.Eat__Pray__Love" title="Eat, Pray, Love by Elizabeth Gilbert" rel="nofollow noopener">eat pray love</a>, EG meets the older brazilian "felipe" in bali and falls in love. ultimately, they wish to settle in the US, near EG's beloved family. but they have decided to never marry because they have both been through awful divorces. felipe has been leaving the US every 90 days for work, then returning, and that has been working out fine. until one day, while returning, he is arrested and told that he has worn out his welcome, and the only way he'll be able to return to the states is if he &amp; EG get hitched.<br /><br />EG &amp; felipe head to southeast asia, where they can live cheaply together while they wait for all the paperwork to go through. EG researches and writes as a way to process her thoughts &amp; confusions about matrimony. it is obvious from the get-go that this is what will happen for this couple to stay together. so, it's not so much about convincing EG to get married a second time as it is about convincing EG that being married can be different this second time.<br /><br />so EG sets off to writes a history of marriage as it interests and applies to her personally. i realize that this is deeply irksome to people who are not very similar to her, but to be fair: she does warn the reader several times that this is exactly what she is doing. she is researching marriage in southeastern asia because that is where she is traveling. she is researching marriage as it pertains to feminists because she is a feminist. she is researching childless marriage/childless women because she does not want to have children (perhaps my favorite part of the book.) she writes about gay marriage because she realizes that people dear to her who are gay, if in the same situation as she &amp; felipe find themselves, would not be able to solve things by getting married.<br /><br />as a feminist childless homo-sympathizer in a happy marriage, i loved the messages of this book, perhaps in an irrational, unfair way. i've already signed the paperwork and had the ceremony, so what could be more fun than 300 pages affirming my decisions and beliefs? but seriously, i do think there are other women who struggle with these issues. i also love EG's voice and writing style: compulsively readable with dry humor. i do wish she had done a better job citing her sources- i want to follow up on some of this stuff and the vague listing in the acknowledgements doesn't help that much. in a few years i will probably read this again and re-evaluate how pertinent it is to my life. but for now: spot on refreshing deliciousness.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11316222155417201154" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_75999390" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/75999390" />
    <a title="Mandy Sue" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1410084-mandy-sue"><img alt="Mandy Sue" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523283327p2/1410084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/75999390?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mandy Sue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mandy Sue" href="/user/show/1410084-mandy-sue">Mandy Sue</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1410084-mandy-sue?shelf=biography-memoir">biography-memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1410084-mandy-sue?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1410084-mandy-sue?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer75999390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13578493238500761534">I find it insulting (maybe insulting is a harsh word...disappointing, maybe?) to readers that Ms. Gilbert or "Mrs. Brazilian Felipe" can change the way she portrays herself in two memoirs and expect the readers to embrace it.<br/><br/>In <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19501.Eat__Pray__Love' title='Eat, Pray, Love by Elizabeth Gilbert' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eat, Pray, Love</a>, Liz portrayed herself as a spiritual person looking to better herself after self destructing (although I didn't feel that way about her situation until reading Committed) her first marriage. The readers loved her yearning for self discovery; some to the p</span>
  <span id="freeText13578493238500761534" style="display:none">I find it insulting (maybe insulting is a harsh word...disappointing, maybe?) to readers that Ms. Gilbert or "Mrs. Brazilian Felipe" can change the way she portrays herself in two memoirs and expect the readers to embrace it.<br /><br />In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19501.Eat__Pray__Love" title="Eat, Pray, Love by Elizabeth Gilbert" rel="nofollow noopener">Eat, Pray, Love</a>, Liz portrayed herself as a spiritual person looking to better herself after self destructing (although I didn't feel that way about her situation until reading Committed) her first marriage. The readers loved her yearning for self discovery; some to the point where they tried to copy her exact route in order to find the same balance at the ending. In Committed, the only way Liz portrays herself is as a selfish, childish, feminist, nonconformist who can't fathom complying to any set of rules.<br /><br />The first half of Committed is mostly history and statistics which being a history and religious buff, I highly enjoyed... and then Liz seeped through. Not in a spiritual, guided way; but that of a 3 year old child having a temper tantrum because she can't have things her way.<br /><br /> This book was a disappointment. Not just in her obsessive quoting, statistics and random ramblings about things she has read on the history of matrimony but a disappointment to readers who read EPL and mistook her childish escape to these countries as a search for self discovery.<br /><br />Liz didn't go to Italy, India and Indonesia in EPL for spiritual guidance or to better herself. She went to hide in these places from the difficulties of divorce and didn't go back until she thought the "coast was clear." <br /><br />Then after she left it all behind, she once again found something else she could rant and complain about....Marriage. Which is exactly what this book is: A childish rant, trying to justify her reasons to avoid conforming to the norm of marriage and parenting.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13578493238500761534" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_84313108" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/84313108" />
    <a title="Annie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1851966-annie"><img alt="Annie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294681265p2/1851966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/84313108?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie" href="/user/show/1851966-annie">Annie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1851966-annie?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1851966-annie?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer84313108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16686221276299021154">I picked this up to review. I almost put it back down again, because it seems like everyone and her uncle has reviewed this book in print, but I didn't have anything else to replace it with, so I thought I'd try anyway.<br/><br/>I'm glad I did. For some reason, I picked up on things the other reviewers didn't. Well, maybe it's not that they didn't notice, but it didn't matter to them.<br/><br/>As a memoir, this isn't the greatest, but then again I don't like memoirs in the first place. As a book using one relations</span>
  <span id="freeText16686221276299021154" style="display:none">I picked this up to review. I almost put it back down again, because it seems like everyone and her uncle has reviewed this book in print, but I didn't have anything else to replace it with, so I thought I'd try anyway.<br /><br />I'm glad I did. For some reason, I picked up on things the other reviewers didn't. Well, maybe it's not that they didn't notice, but it didn't matter to them.<br /><br />As a memoir, this isn't the greatest, but then again I don't like memoirs in the first place. As a book using one relationship to help frame a cultural study of marriage, it was great. I love all the research Gilbert put into this, from marriage ceremonies in Laos to statistics from a Rutgers study to the mating habits of seagulls and the letters of Chekov. It's a magpie collection of information, and I love that. <br /><br />It's the parts where she becomes too personal and too self-conscious about being personal that tends to drag the book down. And when I write "personal," I don't mean the nitty-gritty of her sex life. I mean her spending pages on a list of pros and cons and self-examination for making one decision to go to Cambodia. Sure, it is later related to a larger theme, but it's done awkwardly and too slowly. She spends too much time justifying herself, I think. Of course, she freely admits that this entire book was written in order to justify herself. The other bits are good, though, and made it worth reading.<br /><br />Especially the re-telling of Plato's theory on why we desire to complete ourselves with another person. I now have to return to Plato.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16686221276299021154" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5887725058908238729"> was fully prepared to not like this book. <div id="review_87786960" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87786960" />
    <a title="Irish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1198706-irish"><img alt="Irish" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87786960?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irish" href="/user/show/1198706-irish">Irish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1198706-irish?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87786960" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11147893908110760159">Love, true love, has brought us together today<br/><br/>I finished <a href='http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0670021652/ref=s9_simi_gw_p14_i1?pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&pf_rd_s=center-2&pf_rd_r=06ER7C0HS3WD6XKZWGW9&pf_rd_t=101&pf_rd_p=470938631&pf_rd_i=507846' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Committed</a>, and am at an understanding with the book. I would say this book is worth a read, but as a reader, one must be committed to the book. A reader has to go into this book with an open mind (a few of Gilbert's views may be too liberal for some) and a reader absolutely must finish the book. This is not the type of book one can pick up, read a few chapters of and then put down. You'll walk away with an incomplete viewpoint and it isn't</span>
  <span id="freeText11147893908110760159" style="display:none">Love, true love, has brought us together today<br /><br />I finished <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0670021652/ref=s9_simi_gw_p14_i1?pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&amp;pf_rd_s=center-2&amp;pf_rd_r=06ER7C0HS3WD6XKZWGW9&amp;pf_rd_t=101&amp;pf_rd_p=470938631&amp;pf_rd_i=507846" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Committed</a>, and am at an understanding with the book. I would say this book is worth a read, but as a reader, one must be committed to the book. A reader has to go into this book with an open mind (a few of Gilbert's views may be too liberal for some) and a reader absolutely must finish the book. This is not the type of book one can pick up, read a few chapters of and then put down. You'll walk away with an incomplete viewpoint and it isn't fair to you nor is it fair to Gilbert to not finish this book once you start it. In this way, the book itself is an excellent metaphor to marriage and relationships.<br /><br />So, why did I read the book? There were no imminent questions about marriage in my life requiring reflection. Italian and I are happy in our marriage and have really grown up together, supporting each other along the way. Honestly, I picked up the book because I wanted to know if Elizabeth got married. Why did I care? Because it seemed obvious to me they were in love at the end of <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Eat-Pray-Love-Everything-Indonesia/dp/0143038419/ref=ntt_at_ep_dpi_2" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19501.Eat__Pray__Love" title="Eat, Pray, Love by Elizabeth Gilbert" rel="nofollow noopener">Eat, Pray, Love</a>. That was it. <br /><br />The book, then, was a surprise in its discourse on the institute of marriage, and I realized while reading it that I have also separated the concepts of being bound by love to another person and the social construct of legally binding two people into a specialized contract. I've viewed the contractual arrangement of marriage and the aspects of love and intimacy as two distinct parts of being married, and they happen at different times. Sometimes, one is even missing.<br /><br />Overall, without "giving away" the book and without betraying the intimate aspects of my marriage, I would say Gilbert's book is a modern look at marriage and her reflection on the topic is at a level often missing in today's world. Just like a good marriage, if you start it, you do have to invest time into it, hearing out her arguments, and seeing how she finds peace. For those getting married, it's a good read to spark discussion. For those married, it's a good read to spark discussion. For those contemplating if they ever want to get married, I think this book will be especially poignant. Getting married is a very public display of an extremely personally decision, and Gilbert's public display of her struggle with the decision may be relevant or insightful.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11147893908110760159" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_97468947" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97468947" />
    <a title="Rebekah O&#39;Dell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/138010-rebekah-o-dell"><img alt="Rebekah O&#39;Dell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498857366p2/138010.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97468947?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebekah O&#39;Dell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebekah O&#39;Dell" href="/user/show/138010-rebekah-o-dell">Rebekah O&#39;Dell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97468947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9396962861942255722"> I don’t envy Elizabeth Gilbert the task of following-up Eat, Pray, Love. The book is so popular and so uber-beloved that Julia Roberts herself is playing Gilbert in the hotly anticipated film adaption, for goodness sake! Aside from an Oprah endorsement (though it has that, too), what more could a book ask for than Julia Roberts’ guffaw attached to it? <br/><br/>But, here it is — Gilbert’s big follow-up. In the “love” section of Eat, Pray, Love, Gilbert meets and falls for Brazilian Felipe while traveling</span>
  <span id="freeText9396962861942255722" style="display:none"> I don’t envy Elizabeth Gilbert the task of following-up Eat, Pray, Love. The book is so popular and so uber-beloved that Julia Roberts herself is playing Gilbert in the hotly anticipated film adaption, for goodness sake! Aside from an Oprah endorsement (though it has that, too), what more could a book ask for than Julia Roberts’ guffaw attached to it? <br /><br />But, here it is — Gilbert’s big follow-up. In the “love” section of Eat, Pray, Love, Gilbert meets and falls for Brazilian Felipe while traveling in Bali. When we rejoin Gilbert in Committed, their relationship has both intensified and solidified. Elizabeth + Felipe = true love. Sadder-but-wiser from their respective nasty divorces, the duo vow to love each other passionately and to never, under any circumstances, get married.<br /><br />Until U.S. Immigration services gets involved and bans Felipe from entry into the United States. Their best advice? Get married. As Gilbert puts it, an engagement “more like something out of Kafka than out of Austen” (19).<br /><br />While they battle the red tape of FBI investigations and immigration interviews, Felipe and Gilbert stay in limbo by traveling around southeast asia. Gilbert, ever the journalist, uses her travels as an opportunity to extensively study not only the history of marriage, but also the sociological and anthropological implications of marriage in cultures and religions around the globe.<br /><br />Let me just say — what she finds out is fascinating. Most of the book can be summed up in the book’s subtitle — Gilbert making peace with the institution of marriage. More non-fiction than memoir (although there are strong memoir overtones), Gilbert dives deep into what makes marriage tick, what makes it disastrous, and how we as a culture have arrived at our assumptions concerning matrimony (like, for example, the fact it’s called “matrimony” and not “patrimony” — the mother-making aspect of marriage is assumed in its very title!).<br /><br />Interestingly, when my friends and I read Eat, Pray, Love, we were unanimous in our enthusiasm for “Eat” and “Pray”….but not so much for “Love”. In our reading, Gilbert loses something of herself again when she meets Felipe, and the book as a slightly more fairy-tale esque ending than felt warrented. (I realize it was a true story … there’s not a lot she could do about that. ) Thus, I approached Committed with trepidation. But I fell in love with funny, honest Gilbert all over again — in fact, I found the newly-found, self-confident Gilbert in Committed more likeable than her seeking <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19501.Eat__Pray__Love" title="Eat, Pray, Love by Elizabeth Gilbert" rel="nofollow noopener">Eat, Pray, Love</a> counterpart. A speedy, informative, funny read, Gilbert’s fans will not be disappointed!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9396962861942255722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_132848028" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132848028" />
    <a title="Cheri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/106692-cheri"><img alt="Cheri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601402708p2/106692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132848028?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheri" href="/user/show/106692-cheri">Cheri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132848028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12028360512926496698">After reading Eat, Pray, Love, I kept waiting for this to get better, for the writing to sound less like an assignment, but it never did. If you're looking for 8,000 reasons why getting married isn't a terrifying idea, might actually be a good thing for you despite the fact that you really don't want to (or you really do, but you just can't bring yourself to admit it), this is the book for you. If you are looking for some reassurance why getting married is a good idea when you really are terrifi</span>
  <span id="freeText12028360512926496698" style="display:none">After reading Eat, Pray, Love, I kept waiting for this to get better, for the writing to sound less like an assignment, but it never did. If you're looking for 8,000 reasons why getting married isn't a terrifying idea, might actually be a good thing for you despite the fact that you really don't want to (or you really do, but you just can't bring yourself to admit it), this is the book for you. If you are looking for some reassurance why getting married is a good idea when you really are terrified of marrying someone you claim to love, then I'm not sure that's what you'll get out of this. A sense of camaraderie, perhaps, but I don't think anything about this book is meant to reassure anyone that marriage is a good idea, for anyone. <br /><br />I don't think the writing itself lives up to Eat, Pray, Love which had at least a cohesive flow. Committed comes across as scattered, grabbing bits and pieces in a desperate attempt to appear to assure herself that there is hope for marriage, while at the same time managing to assure herself that she was right all along in fearing the whole idea of such ridiculous nonsense.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="12028360512926496698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_94014107" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/94014107" />
    <a title="Joan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/595288-joan"><img alt="Joan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194803234p2/595288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/94014107?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joan" href="/user/show/595288-joan">Joan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those contemplating marriage</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/595288-joan?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/595288-joan?shelf=personal-memoir">personal-memoir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94014107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9258059830092968734">I found Elizabeth Gilbert's first book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19501.Eat__Pray__Love' title='Eat, Pray, Love by Elizabeth Gilbert' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eat, Pray, Love</a>, a bit too self-indulgent for my taste. This book, though, struck a better balance of self-indulgent musing and researched social commentary. (And, I use the term "researched" loosely.) If you are contemplating marriage or are just interested in the institution of marriage in Western culture, this is a decent read.</span>
  <span id="freeText9258059830092968734" style="display:none">I found Elizabeth Gilbert's first book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19501.Eat__Pray__Love" title="Eat, Pray, Love by Elizabeth Gilbert" rel="nofollow noopener">Eat, Pray, Love</a>, a bit too self-indulgent for my taste. This book, though, struck a better balance of self-indulgent musing and researched social commentary. (And, I use the term "researched" loosely.) If you are contemplating marriage or are just interested in the institution of marriage in Western culture, this is a decent read.</span>

<div id="review_1445703200" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1445703200" />
    <a title="Sharon Metcalf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49089020-sharon-metcalf"><img alt="Sharon Metcalf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451815807p2/49089020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1445703200?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon Metcalf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon Metcalf" href="/user/show/49089020-sharon-metcalf">Sharon Metcalf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408805763" href="/book/show/7457372-committed">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49089020-sharon-metcalf?shelf=2014-2015">2014-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1445703200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12909353357665961482">I literally snatched this book off the shelf the moment I set eyes upon the authors name, knowing that I would buy it regardless of what it was about. To read the back and discover in the first sentence that this was a continuation of Eat, Pray, Love sealed the deal. I didn't read any further and simply paid the big bucks (yep another $1 bites the dust). What I can say about this book is that is wasn't strictly biographical although the parts that dealt with the story of Liz and Felipe were thor</span>
  <span id="freeText12909353357665961482" style="display:none">I literally snatched this book off the shelf the moment I set eyes upon the authors name, knowing that I would buy it regardless of what it was about. To read the back and discover in the first sentence that this was a continuation of Eat, Pray, Love sealed the deal. I didn't read any further and simply paid the big bucks (yep another $1 bites the dust). What I can say about this book is that is wasn't strictly biographical although the parts that dealt with the story of Liz and Felipe were thoroughly enjoyable; it was definitely a work of non-fiction. It was a part historical, part philosophical, record of matrimony. Liz and Felipe had both been through nasty divorces so when they fell in love they made a vow to each other that they would never marry. They performed their own promise ceremony and swapped rings but they steadfastly never intended to be legally wed. The trouble with that plan was that Liz lived in the USA, Felipe was Brazilian and in order to continue sharing their lives together he had to keep leaving the States every 90 days for a few weeks before he could return. On one fateful return Felipe was taken into custody and spent 6 hours in interogation before being arrested and thrown into jail and unceremoniously evicted (not deported) from the country. They were told the only solution, if they wanted to be together in America, which they obviously did, was to marry. Whilst begrudgingly accepting this as their only avenue to getting the life they wanted together, Liz needed to work through her concerns about the whole ideal of marriage. It was an informative and mostly intersting read full of interesting points and perspectives. It wasn't necessarily an easy read and I didn't feel passionately about this book as I did about the first one of hers I had read. Having said that, even today whilst I was still only mid way through this book I purchased a work of fiction by Elizabeth Gilbert. It seems as though it will be a deviation from the contemorary romances I've so enjoyed but I love the way she writes and I'm willing to give it a chance.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12909353357665961482" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Laine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/757195-laine"><img alt="Laine" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/86612778?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laine" href="/user/show/757195-laine">Laine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer86612778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3544056595861660232">Can you believe I am actually reading this? My curiousity has won out. And of course I am immediately confused by this woman. She wrote this book just for 25 friends/neighbors? How is it this author thinks it is OK to write "I only care about what these 25 people think," and then gets this thing published? Why did she bother? Surely there are Kinkos in New Jersey.<br/>Her broad sweeping generalizations must be viewed as the opinion of a writer who is not considerate enough of her readers to reference</span>
  <span id="freeText3544056595861660232" style="display:none">Can you believe I am actually reading this? My curiousity has won out. And of course I am immediately confused by this woman. She wrote this book just for 25 friends/neighbors? How is it this author thinks it is OK to write "I only care about what these 25 people think," and then gets this thing published? Why did she bother? Surely there are Kinkos in New Jersey.<br />Her broad sweeping generalizations must be viewed as the opinion of a writer who is not considerate enough of her readers to reference and source everything. She would have failed college courses using this method. An index would have been like dying and going to heaven. No, a fair inclusion of the role of women and marriage in the East would have been like dying and going to heaven. I wonder if she chose to ignore all of that data in her three years of research so that her Democratic worldview is not too upset.<br />A conservative estimate of the number of times she explains conservative would have to be, say, conservatively, 25. (there is that number again). (And remember the real "enemy" is a conservative). Here she clearly also "had(s) this story deliciously backwards the whole time." How could she get away with constantly slamming conservatives and not once (I believe) actually even mention or use the word liberal? This is like writing about hot, and never mentioning cold. Or up, and never mentioning down. In, and never mentioning out. Oh yes, or West, and never investigating East, maybe? <br />She is just so immature/wrong/blockheaded/tiresome on so many things, but I am happy to report I see some improvements from the last one. Other readers will probably notice all of those as well. And, of course, I am hopeful she will continue to grow.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3544056595861660232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('g3xGXK+HM4spbWUELtQS4M5HFYCdnUcZ+/ZoMq1wfKGKMJFFe1LO8q3qaKvM3f43YMpZAuolHitbj4jtGfKJjQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_52129515'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/52129515-untamed?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Untamed<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/17099759.Glennon_Doyle?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Glennon Doyle<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.13 avg rating &mdash; 123,177 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2020\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer4454636260991812172\">There is a voice of longing inside every woman. Instead, it leaves us feeling weary, stuck, o<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText4454636260991812172\" style=\"display:none\">There is a voice of longing inside every woman. We strive so mightily to be good: good mothers, daughters, partners, employees, citizens, and friends. We believe all this striving will make us feel alive. Instead, it leaves us feeling weary, stuck, overwhelmed, and underwhelmed. We look at our lives, relationships, and world, and wonder: Wasn’t it all supposed to be more beautiful than this?\n\nFour years ago, Glennon Doyle, author, activist and humanitarian, wife and mother of three—was speaking at a conference when a woman entered the room. Marital bliss is possible, she says, if each partner is blissful apart from the other.\n  A fascinating window on the many faces of modern relationships, The Secret Lives of Wives brims with inspiring and daring examples of women who have it both ways: a committed marriage and personal adventures in uncharted territory. Чудесна възможност, нали? Само че има едно условие – трябва да поправите своя фатална грешка. Не ви казват каква е тя, а вие не помните нищо – нито за себе си, нито за живота си. \nАлексей получава този шанс и приема предизвикателството. Но за да поправи миналото, той трябва да се превъплъти последователно в трима души и да избере живота на един от тях за следващите 33 години. Трима души, загинали едновременно от ръката на убиец. \n„Ти си умрял, по-точно си убит. Но ти не си единствената жертва. По същото време са убити още няколко души. Ти не помниш, разбира се, кой от всички си бил – иначе играта нямаше да има смисъл. Вероятно всеки от убитите би искал да разполага с твоя избор...\nДавам ти шанс. Онзи втори шанс, за който всички вие така отчаяно се молите. Ти ще живееш по девет дни като всеки един от тримата убити. Постарай се да ги разбереш и да ги обикнеш. Или пък да ги намразиш... каквото се получи. После ще се върнеш тук и ще направиш своя избор – ще посочиш в чий образ искаш да продължиш да живееш.“\nС изтрити за земното си минало спомени, Алексей изживява последните девет дни на всеки от тях. Време, наситено с емоции и разтърсващи събития, които изправят героите на кръстопът.\n„Играта“ се оказва сложна и пълна с изкушения и екзистенциални въпроси. А накрая Алексей е изправен пред огромната тежест на свободния избор.\nДали Алексей ще разпознае себе си в някоя от трите жертви и чий живот ще избере? Дали ще успее да преначертае миналото? Как ще види света през очите на други хора?\nПредставяме ви известния руски писател Олег Рой с романа „Фантомна болка“. Един философски роман за човешката същност, за доброто и злото и за неуловимата граница между ада и рая в самите нас. За грешките, които правим, и за шанса да започнем отначало. За любовта и прошката. И за отговорността на свободния избор.\n\nВ Русия са продадени над един милион книжни копия от романа „Фантомна болка“, който заема първо място в топ 10 романа на Олег Рой.<\/span>\n  <a Young women live by feminism\'s goals, yet feminism itself is undeniably at a crossroads; &quot;girl power&quot; feminists appear to be obsessed with personal empowerment at the expense of politics while political institutions such as Ms. and NOW are so battle weary they\'ve lost their ability to speak to a new generation. In Manifesta, Jennifer Baumgardner and Amy Richards show the snags in each feminist hub--from the dissolution of riot grrrls into the likes of the Spice Girls, to older women\'s hawking of young girls\' imperiled self-esteem, to the hyped hatred of feminist thorns like Katie Roiphe and Naomi Wolf--and prove that these snags have not, in fact, torn feminism asunder. In an intelligent and incendiary argument, Baumgardner and Richards address issues instead of feelings and the political as well as the personal. They describe the seven deadly sins the media commits against feminism, provide keys to accessible and urgent activism, discuss why the ERA is still a relevant and crucial political goal, and spell out what a world with equality would look like. Swayed by his friends\' ridicule, he has his new truck painted white to cover the vibrant turquoise, once his favorite color. Soon, he realizes his mistake. &quot;I\'d done exactly what my dad had told me not to. I\'d listened to other people\'s opinions instead of listening to what I\'d felt inside.&quot; So begins this poignant and moving account of Villasenor\'s coming of age. Growing up on his parents\' ranch in North San Diego County, Victor Villasenor\'s teenage years were marked by a painful quest to find a place for himself in a world he didn\'t fit into. During his search, Victor wrangles with the usual questions of adolescence: Is it normal to think about sex all the time? Do good girls like sex? Is sex before marriage a sin? But Victor struggles with more than just his burgeoning sexual awareness. The son of a self-made, successful man, he is different from his peers because of his Mexican heritage, and the experiences both subtle and outright discrimination because of this. Raised in a tight-knit, Catholic family, he questions the tenets of his Catholic faith and the restrictions it places on his own developing spirituality. After high school, Victor\'s quest for &quot;whohe is and who he isn\'t&quot; takes him to Mexico, where he is shocked to learn that Mexicans--aside from his father--are successful. They are architects, professors, and artists. This incredible revelation allows him to appreciate his own potential and realize his dreams of making a difference in the world through writing. A powerful portrait of a young boy on the path to manhood in the shadow of his influential father, Crazy Loco Love adds a new chapter to the grand tradition of coming-of-age books. Destined to become a classic, this new installment in Villasenor\'s body of work confirms his place as a leading American writer. Crazy Loco Love will enthrall his many fans and surely win him new ones.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"14248375876857928202\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/11679.Elizabeth_Gilbert">About Elizabeth Gilbert</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/11679.Elizabeth_Gilbert"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1440718929p3/11679.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/11679.Elizabeth_Gilbert">Elizabeth Gilbert
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
27,320
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1324679730446109113"><br/><b>Elizabeth Gilbert</b> is an award-winning writer of both fiction and non-fiction. Her short story collection <i>Pilgrims</i> was a finalist for the PEN/Hemingway award, and her novel <i>Stern Men</i> was a New York Times notable book. Her 2002 book The Last American Man was a finalist for both the National Book Award and the National Book Critic’s Circle Award. <br/><br/>Her memoir, <i>Eat, Pray, Love</i>, spent 57 weeks in the #1 </span>
  <span id="freeText1324679730446109113" style="display:none"><br /><b>Elizabeth Gilbert</b> is an award-winning writer of both fiction and non-fiction. Her short story collection <i>Pilgrims</i> was a finalist for the PEN/Hemingway award, and her novel <i>Stern Men</i> was a New York Times notable book. Her 2002 book The Last American Man was a finalist for both the National Book Award and the National Book Critic’s Circle Award. <br /><br />Her memoir, <i>Eat, Pray, Love</i>, spent 57 weeks in the #1 spot on the New York Times paperback bestseller list. It has shipped over 6 million copies in the US and has been published in over thirty languages. A film adaptation of the book was released by Columbia Pictures with an all star cast: Julia Roberts as Gilbert, Javier Bardem as Felipe, James Franco as David, Billy Crudup as her ex-husband and Richard Jenkins as Richard from Texas.<br /><br />Her latest novel, <i>The Signature of All Things</i>, will be available on October 1, 2013. The credit for her profile picture belongs to Jennifer Schatten. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1324679730446109113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/6924954-committed-a-skeptic-makes-peace-with-marriage">Quotes from Committed: A Skep...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;To be fully seen by somebody, then, and be loved anyhow - this is a human offering that can border on miraculous.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/227010-to-be-fully-seen-by-somebody-then-and-be-loved">2697 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;People always fall in love with the most perfect aspects of each other’s personalities. Who wouldn’t? Anybody can love the most wonderful parts of another person. But that’s not the clever trick. The really clever trick is this: Can you accept the flaws? Can you look at your partner’s faults honestly and say, ‘I can work around that. I can make something out of it.’? Because the good stuff is always going to be there, and it’s always going to pretty and sparkly, but the crap underneath can ruin you.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/278926-people-always-fall-in-love-with-the-most-perfect-aspects">1571 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
